<div id="review_567019344" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567019344" />
    <a title="Kathleen Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1471504-kathleen-valentine"><img alt="Kathleen Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442476724p2/1471504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/567019344?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen Valentine" href="/user/show/1471504-kathleen-valentine">Kathleen Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer567019344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12428279304996380555">I thought this was an absolutely astonishing story. The writing is deep, and, though there were many times when I thought it seemed to go on a bit, I found myself still caught up in the rhythm of her astonishing prose. The central character, Ariah, is not a very likable character. On the first night of her honeymoon in Niagara Falls in the early 1950s, her new husband leaves their bed, walks to the Falls and throws himself over. Ariah finds the suicide note h left but destroys it without telling</span>
  <span id="freeText12428279304996380555" style="display:none">I thought this was an absolutely astonishing story. The writing is deep, and, though there were many times when I thought it seemed to go on a bit, I found myself still caught up in the rhythm of her astonishing prose. The central character, Ariah, is not a very likable character. On the first night of her honeymoon in Niagara Falls in the early 1950s, her new husband leaves their bed, walks to the Falls and throws himself over. Ariah finds the suicide note h left but destroys it without telling anyone. During the seven days that Ariah keeps watch as police search for his body, a young lawyer, Dirk Burnaby, keeps her company.<br /><br />A month later Ariah is back in Troy, NY when Burnaby shows up, tells her he can't get her out of his mind, and begs her to marry him. She does and they move back to Niagara Falls where Burnaby grew up in a prominent and affluent family. Burnaby's devotion to his wife is both admirable and baffling. They have three children though Ariah is never sure if their first-born son, Chandler, belongs to Dirk or her first husband, however unlikely that may seem. Throughout the years she continually hears stories about the "Widow Bride," the sad young woman whose husband left her on their wedding night and "fell" into the gorge.<br /><br />With three small children and a successful law practice, Dirk makes a difficult decision, he decides to take the case of a group of working class people whose lives are being ruined by mysterious illnesses. They all live in an area known as Love Canal. It is an unfortunate decision because it destroys Dirk's standing in the community, and eventually, his life.<br /><br />The second half of the book is told from the points of view of each of their three children - Chandler, Royall, and Juliet -- as each seeks to find the truth of their father's life.<br /><br />This is a deep, dark, extraordinary book in which the Falls themselves become as much a character within the story as any of the others. It is not a book for everyone but I found it mesmerizing and I'm sure it will haunt me for a very long time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12428279304996380555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_67293418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67293418" />
    <a title="Surreysmum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1153430-surreysmum"><img alt="Surreysmum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1210468201p2/1153430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67293418?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Surreysmum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Surreysmum" href="/user/show/1153430-surreysmum">Surreysmum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1153430-surreysmum?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1153430-surreysmum?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1153430-surreysmum?shelf=waterfalls">waterfalls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1153430-surreysmum?shelf=passed-on">passed-on</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67293418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1957370401140248781">This book met my standard for keeping me engrossed on the subway. Oates is certainly an engaging writer, with a flair for Gothic excess (sex in a graveyard, forsooth). When I saw the story was to be multi-generational, I hoped for a more robust pattern, perhaps along the lines of Wuthering Heights, where the second generation, though repeating some of the happenings of the first generation, has a better outcome. But aside from the said graveyard sex, where the son has a bizarre sexual encounter </span>
  <span id="freeText1957370401140248781" style="display:none">This book met my standard for keeping me engrossed on the subway. Oates is certainly an engaging writer, with a flair for Gothic excess (sex in a graveyard, forsooth). When I saw the story was to be multi-generational, I hoped for a more robust pattern, perhaps along the lines of Wuthering Heights, where the second generation, though repeating some of the happenings of the first generation, has a better outcome. But aside from the said graveyard sex, where the son has a bizarre sexual encounter with a woman who was only suspected of (and did not have) a sexual relationship with the father, I didn't see much of that going on. Instead, the story of the difficult Ariah trifurcates into the stories of her three children, and there is a rather perfunctory-feeling attempt at reunification of both the plots and the family itself at a memorial for the quasi-heroic and misunderstood husband and father.<br /><br />I found the political part of the story - the beginnings of the Love Canal scandal and the rottenness at the heart of the business/political class - laid on *just* thick enough. Any more, and I would have complained that Oates' research was overwhelming the story. On the other hand, the evocation of the Falls themselves, in all their magnificent, romantic and anti-romantic, deadly, mysterious, curiously familiar glory, was wonderful, and I could definitely have lived with more of the same.<br /><br />Anyway, structural complaints aside, I really appreciated the strong imagery and storytelling, and I would most certainly read more by this author (this was my first). </span>
  <a data-text-id="1957370401140248781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_75159644" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75159644" />
    <a title="Marci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/722691-marci"><img alt="Marci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557589924p2/722691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75159644?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marci" href="/user/show/722691-marci">Marci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75159644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10596875134520258068">I've read some complaints about this book as being "over-written" and "boring" with "hard-to-like characters" - and while I can see where these folks are coming from - this is part of what I like about JCO. That she creates a complete & believable world with flawed characters, (who sometimes think in cliche, even - another complaint I read). I enjoy all the details, how JCO creates an image I can actually see. Contrary to what someone in another review complained about, I think it was important </span>
  <span id="freeText10596875134520258068" style="display:none">I've read some complaints about this book as being "over-written" and "boring" with "hard-to-like characters" - and while I can see where these folks are coming from - this is part of what I like about JCO. That she creates a complete &amp; believable world with flawed characters, (who sometimes think in cliche, even - another complaint I read). I enjoy all the details, how JCO creates an image I can actually see. Contrary to what someone in another review complained about, I think it was important to follow Ariah on the morning of and week after her first husband's suicide, how everyone treated and thought of her. I would imagine such details during a hugely important happening that shaped a character and her future would matter. While it's sometimes frustrating that nothing comes from certain details (Ariah hiding the note, Royall's encounter with the woman in black), if not meant as a red herring (annoying) it also resembles real life where not everything is resolved or addressed. And I did find the Niagara history totally enthralling. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10596875134520258068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_326814854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326814854" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/962322-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430584962p2/962322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326814854?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/962322-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326814854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4633593028661312715">Joyce Carol Oates wears me out and this book is no exception. Not only is this this the same Oatsian theme as always, a relatively happy family - none of her families are without problems to begin with - is destroyed by a catastrophic event, but it's set in upstate New York, which is not exactly Thomas Hardy's Wessex. (There is a slight parallel here, though; just as the woods have some protagonism in "The Woodlanders", Niagara Falls exerts a strong influence in this novel.) All of the typical O</span>
  <span id="freeText4633593028661312715" style="display:none">Joyce Carol Oates wears me out and this book is no exception. Not only is this this the same Oatsian theme as always, a relatively happy family - none of her families are without problems to begin with - is destroyed by a catastrophic event, but it's set in upstate New York, which is not exactly Thomas Hardy's Wessex. (There is a slight parallel here, though; just as the woods have some protagonism in "The Woodlanders", Niagara Falls exerts a strong influence in this novel.) All of the typical Oates elements are present here except for rape. (I don't think that counts as a plot spoiler unless that's important for you.) What's missing is any particularly sympathetic character or real cohesion in the story; it felt like a pastiche of plot threads that never came together. There were themes such as latent homosexuality and toxic waste dumps before people knew what these were but most of it just felt half-baked to me. If you haven't read this yet, you really haven't missed out but if you're forced, it isn't a particularly painful time-killer either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4633593028661312715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_253263636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253263636" />
    <a title="Jim Leckband" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4180616-jim-leckband"><img alt="Jim Leckband" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295305256p2/4180616.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253263636?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Leckband" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Leckband" href="/user/show/4180616-jim-leckband">Jim Leckband</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060722289" href="/book/show/228341.The_Falls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253263636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4763910317821771509">I like what Oates did with Niagara Falls in this novel. She acknowledged the Falls' role in popular culture as natural wonder, honeymoon magnet and resort. These facets are in the background as she regards the Falls as a mysterious force. This is never obvious as in a mystery or horror novel, but as a subtle influence on the area and a huge influence on a couple of characters.<br/><br/>The Love Canal connection to the Falls was done very well. I was wary that the novel was going to become "A Civil Action"</span>
  <span id="freeText4763910317821771509" style="display:none">I like what Oates did with Niagara Falls in this novel. She acknowledged the Falls' role in popular culture as natural wonder, honeymoon magnet and resort. These facets are in the background as she regards the Falls as a mysterious force. This is never obvious as in a mystery or horror novel, but as a subtle influence on the area and a huge influence on a couple of characters.<br /><br />The Love Canal connection to the Falls was done very well. I was wary that the novel was going to become "A Civil Action" or "Erin Brockovich" - but it ended not being primarily about Love Canal and the horrible actions of the chemical plants and community. Rather Oates was focused on the characters involved, the lawyer, the plaintiff and the lawyer's family as they started the lawsuit going. <br /><br />All in all, one of the best that I've read of Oates so far (I'm reading the novels in chronological order.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4763910317821771509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873372552?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/3739451-suzanne">Suzanne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=geocaching-challenge-2016">geocaching-challenge-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873372552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8657724267931578044">In the opening pages of the novel, a young red-headed woman wakes to find her groom missing the morning after their wedding.  Honeymooning in the famous Niagara Falls area, scandal soon erupts as news arrives that a man fitting his description has jumped to his death in the falls.<br/><br/>This is a novel that simply brims with excitement and interesting characters.  Oates reels her reader in with not one story line, but several - one after another - in what becomes a saga of this woman's life, the commun</span>
  <span id="freeText8657724267931578044" style="display:none">In the opening pages of the novel, a young red-headed woman wakes to find her groom missing the morning after their wedding.  Honeymooning in the famous Niagara Falls area, scandal soon erupts as news arrives that a man fitting his description has jumped to his death in the falls.<br /><br />This is a novel that simply brims with excitement and interesting characters.  Oates reels her reader in with not one story line, but several - one after another - in what becomes a saga of this woman's life, the community and the lives of her future husband and children.<br /><br />I had no expectations of this book, but was pleasantly surprised by how quickly it captured my interest and didn't let go until the final page.  A great read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8657724267931578044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WlBfPeUORAatMLOEvygGuAcvwMf44bAXryLGvm8NqewaOi0yPoC+Vd/3poqBQTmH9yZ2mm1Xq5zlk+We3vrEhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MUwyxrQ596Zw+c65zLeY6kAQFGcCFl4Xd8ZtuYsKGz5xJkDJb7cN9QI+27fy3qfVsBmiOpegRZw9d06ZOv12Vg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Η ήττα του 1897 ήταν ακόμα νωπή, το καθεστώς ασταθές, άνθιζε η διαφθορά, η εκπαίδευση δεν ανταποκρινόταν στις ευρωπαϊκές αντιλήψεις περί παιδαγωγικής. Από την άλλη, το γλωσσικό ζήτημα έκαιγε. Ο Εκπαιδευτικός Όμιλος, του οποίου ήταν μέλος και η Δέλτα, συσπείρωνε διανοούμενους, όπως λογοτέχνες (Βάρναλης, Καζαντζάκης, Νιρβάνας), εκπαιδευτικούς και παιδαγωγούς (Γληνός, Δελμούζος) φιλολόγους (Σαρής, Τριανταφυλλίδης), με στόχο μεταρρυθμίσεις που αφορούσαν στην εισαγωγή της δημοτικής γλώσσας στην εκπαίδευση και στην εξάπλωση νέων ιδεών για την ανατροφή των παιδιών.\nΜΑΡΙΖΑ ΝΤΕΚΑΣΤΡΟ\n\nΤο &quot;Παραμύθι χωρίς όνομα&quot; είναι ένα πολιτικό παραμύθι, είναι μια πλατωνική Πολιτεία για παιδιά, είναι η ιστορία μιας παραμυθένιας πατρίδας... Της Ελλάδας.\n\nΗ Πηνελόπη Δ. είναι πιστή, όπως τ\' όνομά της, στις ιδέες της μέσα στο βιβλίο, πιστή μέχρι το θάνατο σ\'όλα όσα επέλεξε να ξεχάσει και σ\' αυτά που τόσο μεθοδικά προτείνει.\n\nΤα ονόματα των πρωταγωνιστών τούς ανήκουν εκ φύσεως και διηγούνται κι από μόνα τους την ιστορία. Ο καλός βασιλιάς, που μετρήθηκαν οι μέρες του, λέγεται Συνετός, και μετά αρχίζει η βασιλεία του Αστόχαστου και της Παλάβως στη Χώρα των Μοιρολάτρων. Μέχρι που, από τη γειτονική χώρα, φτάνει, αντί για οικονομική βοήθεια, η ύστατη προσβολή: μια γαϊδουροκεφαλή με τενεκεδένιο στέμμα.\n\nΚι εδώ ακριβώς αρχίζει το παραμύθι για τα απογοητευμένα μάτια μας. Ο γιος του Αστόχαστου λέγεται Συνετός Β΄ και αρκεί να πούμε ότι στο τέλος θα παντρευτεί τη Γνώση, κόρη της Φρόνησης, λες κι έχει πάρει το αξίωμά του κατευθείαν από τον Σωκράτη.\n\nΞαναδιαβάζοντας το βιβλίο, ένας μεγάλος θα νιώσει ίσως αμήχανα στις μέρες μας, αντιμέτωπος μ\'αυτή την ελπίδα που δεν διαψεύδεται και με την αρετή που ξαναχτίζει τον κόσμο - χωρίς καθόλου μαγικά ξόρκια ή δανεικά κονδύλια, αλλά χάρη σε πολύ σκληρή δουλειά για το κοινό καλό. Γιατί ένας μεγάλος αυτόματα θα μετρήσει την απόσταση ανάμεσα σ\' αυτά που επέλεξε να υποτιμήσει και να ξεχάσει και στα τόσα που μεθοδικά προτείνει το βιβλίο. Γιατί η Πηνελόπη Δ. έχει προβλέψει ακόμα και για τη σωστή εκμετάλλευση της φύσης, έχει σκεφτεί ακόμα και τους φυλακισμένους να ξανακάνει ανθρώπους μέσα από την πιο σκληρή, είναι η αλήθεια, δουλειά των λατομείων. Και παρόλο που δεν ξεφεύγει από την παρουσία μιας ελέω Θεού βασιλικής οικογένειας, το βασιλόπουλο είναι τόσο ταπεινό, εργατικό και ενάρετο που θα μπορούσε να είναι ένας αυτοδημιούργητος λαϊκός ήρωας.\nΜΑΡΙΑ ΜΗΤΣΟΡΑ\n\nΗ Πηνελόπη Δέλτα φώτισε τα παιδικά μας χρόνια, τα κατοίκησε και τα ενθάρρυνε δίνοντας &quot;όνομα&quot; -και μια σπάνια αύρα- στα ανείπωτα της ψυχής. Κι αν η γενιά μας στρέφει ακόμη το βλέμμα της νοσταλγικά σ\' εκείνα τα αναγνώσματα, οι τάξεις των νεόκοπων αναγνωστών ούτε λιγότερο πυκνές είναι ούτε λιγότερο ένθερμες.\nΖΥΡΑΝΝΑ ΖΑΤΕΛΗ\n\nΤο &quot;Παραμύθι χωρίς όνομα&quot; (πρώτη έκδοση: 1910) αποτελεί πραγματικά το πιο συναρπαστικό εγερτήριο σάλπισμα για μια Ελλάδα της εργατικότητας, της τιμιότητας, της προκοπής, της μόρφωσης, της εθνικής περηφάνειας. In ancient times, people thought that the Sun, Moon, and stars were gods. They recorded their movements and imagined that the stars made pictures in the sky. The Greeks and the Romans related these &quot;pictures&quot; of animals and men—or constellations—to their legends. They also identified planets and named them for their gods—Venus, Mars, Saturn, and Jupiter. Their observations marked the first step in the development of astronomy, which today is a sophisticated science. Modern astronomers have followed the tradition of naming heavenly bodies after ancient gods. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10083226455932952482">Joyce Carol Oates is a recipient of the National Book Award and the PEN/Malamud Award for Excellence in Short Fiction. She is also the recipient of the 2005 Prix Femina for The Falls. She is the Roger S. Berlind Distinguished Professor of the Humanities at Princeton University, and she has been a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters since 1978. Pseudonyms ... <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/107067.Rosamond_Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rosamond Smith</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/254977.Lauren_Kelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laure</a></span>
  <span id="freeText10083226455932952482" style="display:none">Joyce Carol Oates is a recipient of the National Book Award and the PEN/Malamud Award for Excellence in Short Fiction. She is also the recipient of the 2005 Prix Femina for The Falls. She is the Roger S. Berlind Distinguished Professor of the Humanities at Princeton University, and she has been a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters since 1978.
